    <section class="posts"> 
     <article class="post single-post"> 
      <header class="post-header"> 
       <h1><a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/">Web browser released!</a></h1> 
       <div class="post-meta-container"> 
        <ul class="post-meta"> 
         <li class="author"><a href="/author/eben">Eben Upton</a></li> 
         <li class="date"><a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/">1st Sep 2014</a></li> 
         <li class="num-comments"><a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comments" class="open-comments-top">250 Comments</a></li> 
        </ul> 
       </div> 
      </header> 
      <div class="entry-content"> 
       <p><i>Update: Marco Barisione, who led the browser work at Collabora has written a <a href="http://blog.barisione.org/2014-09/rpi-browser/">blog post</a> about it.</i></p> 
       <p>Back in December 2013, we <a href="http://www.raspberrypi.org/web-browser-beta/">discussed</a> our plans to develop an improved web browser for Raspberry Pi. The browser is based on <a href="https://wiki.gnome.org/Apps/Web">Epiphany</a> (aka GNOME Web), as a replacement for the rather venerable version of Midori in Raspbian Wheezy.</p> 
       <p>Eight months and a lot of hard work later, we’re finally ready. As you can see from the video below, Epiphany on Pi is now a plausible alternative to a desktop browser for all but the most JavaScript-heavy sites.</p> 
       <p><iframe src="//player.vimeo.com/video/104919646" width="500" height="281" frameborder="0" webkitallowfullscreen mozallowfullscreen allowfullscreen></iframe></p> 
       <p>Epiphany brings a host of neat features to Raspberry Pi, including:</p> 
       <ul> 
        <li>Much-improved HTML5 support</li> 
        <li>A JavaScript JIT</li> 
        <li><b>Hardware-accelerated video decoding</b></li> 
        <li>ARMv6-optimized blitting functions</li> 
        <li>Better interactivity during page loading</li> 
        <li>Faster scrolling</li> 
       </ul> 
       <p>Future releases of Raspbian and NOOBS will include Epiphany as the default browser, but the necessary packages are already in our repository. To install, type:</p> 
       <pre class="terminal">sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-get dist-upgrade
sudo apt-get install epiphany-browser</pre> 
       <p>Epiphany for Raspberry Pi was produced by our friends at <a href="http://www.collabora.com/">Collabora</a>. ARM assembly language optimisations were provided (as always) by Ben Avison of <a href="https://www.riscosopen.org/content/">RISC OS Open</a>.</p> 
      </div> 
      <footer class="post-footer">

         </ul>

             <cite class="fn">Eben Upton</cite> 
             <span class="says">says:</span> 
            </div> 
            <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
             <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1005735"> 1st Sep 2014 at 2:47 pm</a> 
            </div> 
            <p>Raspbian is developed by Peter Green and Mike Thompson as a “pure” armv6hf port of upstream Debian, so there’s not much scope for us to invest directly in Raspbian.</p> 
            <p>Where we do invest (a lot) is in developing applications like this one which we include in the Foundation’s Raspbian-based distributions.</p>

                <li class="comment even depth-5" id="comment-1047407"> 
                 <div id="div-comment-1047407" class="comment-body"> 
                  <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
                   <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/0ac37ed674681fe8a97bec699ebb8ab1?s=32&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/0ac37ed674681fe8a97bec699ebb8ab1?s=64&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-32 photo" height="32" width="32"> 
                   <cite class="fn">Arjan Vlek</cite> 
                   <span class="says">says:</span> 
                  </div> 
                  <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
                   <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1047407"> 12th Oct 2014 at 1:39 pm</a> 
                  </div> 
                  <p>Flash for Android worked solely on ARMv7+ CPUs (like Cortex Ax series) and therefore never worked on ARMv6 CPUs (like ARM11xx series) that are also used in the RPi. That makes it impossible to port flash from Android (or Chromebooks) to RPi architecture. The *Only* Flash Player that i have ever seen running on ARMv6 is called “FlashLite Plugin for Android”, it runs on my old HTC Wildfire with ARMv6 / ARM11 CPU. Unfortunately, it is extremely slow / limited and therefore not worth the effort to port to RPi.</p> 
                 </div> </li>

                <p>Chrome has flash support baked in without the need to install the Flash binaries on the system. Windows 8 RT also does this with Internet Explorer 11. So its not as simple as adding Flash to Rasbian / Rasberry PI ARM6 the web browser would need to be programmed to include a flash interpreter. I imagine the reason for this not being done is that even Adobe has seen the end of Flash and is pushing for those who develop sites and apps with its development suite to use HTML5.</p>

             <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1005727"> 1st Sep 2014 at 2:31 pm</a> 
            </div> 
            <p>Yes, HTML5 videos with suitable codecs are already hardware acceletated. In fact, support for YouTube and Vimeo is done by explicitly requesting the HTML5 version instead of Flash.</p> 
            <p>As far as I know Epiphany does not provide a kiosk mode, but since most of the improvements are in libwebkitgtk you can use another application or develop a customized browser yourself which just instantiate one or more <a href="http://webkitgtk.org/reference/webkitgtk/stable/webkitgtk-webkitwebview.html" rel="nofollow">WebKitWebView</a>.</p> 
           </div> 
           <ul class="children"> 
            <li class="comment odd alt depth-3 parent" id="comment-1006175"> 
             <div id="div-comment-1006175" class="comment-body"> 
              <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
               <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/88a0a826353f5fd006863df6011afdc4?s=32&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/88a0a826353f5fd006863df6011afdc4?s=64&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-32 photo" height="32" width="32"> 
               <cite class="fn">hunternet93</cite> 
               <span class="says">says:</span> 
              </div> 
              <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
               <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1006175"> 2nd Sep 2014 at 2:35 am</a> 
              </div> 
              <p>For kiosk browsing, try WCGBrowser, a lightweight WebKit browser written in Python: <a href="https://github.com/alandmoore/wcgbrowser" rel="nofollow">https://github.com/alandmoore/wcgbrowser</a> It runs pretty well on the Pi, although won’t have all the improvements put in to Epiphany (unless they’ve been backported to WebKit).</p> 
             </div> 
             <ul class="children"> 
              <li class="comment even depth-4" id="comment-1006396"> 
               <div id="div-comment-1006396" class="comment-body"> 
                <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
                 <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/e6085b498443e8f3888cd07424bb3215?s=32&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/e6085b498443e8f3888cd07424bb3215?s=64&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-32 photo" height="32" width="32"> 
                 <cite class="fn"><a href="https://www.collabora.com" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Emanuele Aina</a></cite> 
                 <span class="says">says:</span> 
                </div> 
                <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
                 <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1006396"> 2nd Sep 2014 at 9:45 am</a> 
                </div> 
                <p>WCGBrowser uses the old Qt port of WebKit (Qt moved to Blink and the Qt port is no longer upstreame) so no, it won’t benefit from the WebKit improvements as they only apply to the GTK+ port. If you happen to know another kiosk application using WebKitGTK+ then it would benefit from the work done as for the most part it applies to underlying libwebkitgtk library rather than to Epiphany.</p> 
               </div> </li>
              <!-- #comment-## --> 
             </ul>
             <!-- .children --> </li>

               <div id="div-comment-1008892" class="comment-body"> 
                <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
                 <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/6fffc4867cee9e6a0120b3ff08ab624e?s=32&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/6fffc4867cee9e6a0120b3ff08ab624e?s=64&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-32 photo" height="32" width="32"> 
                 <cite class="fn"><a href="http://www.barisione.org/" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Marco Barisione</a></cite> 
                 <span class="says">says:</span> 
                </div> 
                <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
                 <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1008892"> 5th Sep 2014 at 2:35 pm</a> 
                </div> 
                <p>The only cause of freezes I’ve seen is JavaScript. When a single block of JS is executed it cannot be stopped in a single-process browser. On a lot of pages there’s quite a bit of JS executed on load, so maybe you are going back, some JS is executed and the browser freezes for a second or so.<br> WebKit2 solves this problem in the Chrome way using multiple processes, but the multiple processes would be too much for the Pi.</p> 
               </div> </li>

                <p>Weird. Maybe you got unlucky an the mirror redirector choose a broken mirror?</p> 
                <p>If that’s the case you may try again to see it the broken mirror has been removed from the pool.</p> 
                <p>Trying one of the URL from my system I correctly get a 302 Redirect:</p> 
                <p><code><br> $ curl -I http://mirrordirector.raspbian.org/raspbian/pool/main/g/gnome-desktop3/gnome-desktop3-data_3.4.2-1_all.deb<br> HTTP/1.1 302 Found<br> ...<br> Location: http://mirror.internetone.it/raspbian/raspbian/pool/main/g/gnome-desktop3/gnome-desktop3-data_3.4.2-1_all.deb<br> </code></p> 
                <p>Trying the destination URL I get a successful response:<br> <code><br> curl -I http://mirror.internetone.it/raspbian/raspbian/pool/main/g/gnome-desktop3/gnome-desktop3-data_3.4.2-1_all.deb<br> HTTP/1.1 200 OK<br> </code></p>

              <li class="comment even depth-4" id="comment-1008582"> 
               <div id="div-comment-1008582" class="comment-body"> 
                <div class="comment-author vcard">

           <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1005835"> 1st Sep 2014 at 5:48 pm</a> 
          </div> 
          <p>Looks good.<br> How do I get my scratch scripts to auto-open ? I have some tutorials with links to scratch code *.sb, which are downloaded but not executed automaticallay (works in midori).<br> Sample: <a href="http://www.heppg.de/ikg/box/adapter/adapterplatine.actor.html#N10D66" rel="nofollow">http://www.heppg.de/ikg/box/adapter/adapterplatine.actor.html#N10D66</a><br> look for the link ‘Beispielcode’.</p> 
          <p>and another observation: on the side mentioned above, there is an embedded svg labelled “Motor-Platte, Microschalter und Nockenscheibe”. This svg is an overlay of graphics with some texts and lines. When loading the page for the first time, only the overlay is displayed. When loading this in a separate tab, it displays nicely. Then (obviously as data are cached, it is updated correctly when refreshing the page.</p> 
          <p>regards, Gerhard</p>

                <p>I couldn’t agree more:). Also noticed that on some sites, Hexus.net and IMDB for example the backdrops don’t appear. Again I think of this as a bonus, it just means quicker loading and less data transfer and I never look at the backdrops anyway.</p>

                <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
                 <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/e6085b498443e8f3888cd07424bb3215?s=32&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/e6085b498443e8f3888cd07424bb3215?s=64&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-32 photo" height="32" width="32"> 
                 <cite class="fn"><a href="https://www.collabora.com" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Emanuele Aina</a></cite> 
                 <span class="says">says:</span> 
                </div> 
                <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
                 <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1006604"> 2nd Sep 2014 at 4:22 pm</a> 
                </div> 
                <p>You can get the exact sources used to build the epiphany and libwebkitgtk packages with apt-get:</p> 
                <p>apt-get source libwebkitgtk-3.0-0 epiphany-browser</p> 
                <p>The patches will be in the debian/patches subfolder of the extracted source trees (note that dpkg already applies them automatically).</p> 
               </div> </li>

          </div> 
          <p>Not relevant to the epiphany-browser but<br> $ sudo apt-get update<br> $ sudo apt-get dist-upgrade<br> on a fresh raspbian SD card takes several hours so maybe worth letting people know. Presumably there’s an updated image in the pipeline and it may be better (quicker?) to wait for that.</p> 
          <p>PS also, I had a very recent raspbian that I had added jessie to the /etc/apt/sources.list (in order to get python-pil NB please, please put this in wheezy soon!) and after dist-upgrade (which took even longer than several hours!) several things seemed to be broken. $ startx<br> produced a message that /usr/bin/X no longer existed and calls openegl.eglCreateContext() (in pi3d) failed to create a context.</p> 
         </div> 
         <ul class="children"> 
          <li class="comment even depth-2" id="comment-1008953"> 
           <div id="div-comment-1008953" class="comment-body"> 
            <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
             <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/6fffc4867cee9e6a0120b3ff08ab624e?s=32&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/6fffc4867cee9e6a0120b3ff08ab624e?s=64&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-32 photo" height="32" width="32"> 
             <cite class="fn"><a href="http://www.barisione.org/" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Marco Barisione</a></cite> 
             <span class="says">says:</span> 
            </div> 
            <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
             <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1008953"> 5th Sep 2014 at 3:54 pm</a> 
            </div> 
            <p>Wow, do you have a particularly slow SD card? On my class 10 SD card it takes quite a bit to instal, but not hours.<br> You can also try using eatmydata to get apt to be faster. This program will avoid costly syncs to disk for the program you passed on the command line (for instance do “eatmydata apt-get install foo”) with the small risk of actually eating your data in case something goes wrong. (So use only on a card you don’t mind reflashing in case of problems.)</p> 
           </div> </li>

            <p>In theory, yes. In practice I guess it would run so slowly that it would probably require hours if not days for a full boot.</p> 
            <p>Note that the optimization focus for the browser has been to keep it as responsive as possible even when running very CPU intensive tasks, to render pages in tiles to keep scrolling smooth and to use hardware acceleration when playing video contents: just don’t expect to see JS code run faster than on an old Pentium. ;)</p>

          <li class="comment even depth-2 parent" id="comment-1007717"> 
           <div id="div-comment-1007717" class="comment-body"> 
            <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
             <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/e6085b498443e8f3888cd07424bb3215?s=32&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/e6085b498443e8f3888cd07424bb3215?s=64&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-32 photo" height="32" width="32"> 
             <cite class="fn"><a href="https://www.collabora.com" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Emanuele Aina</a></cite> 
             <span class="says">says:</span> 
            </div> 
            <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
             <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1007717"> 3rd Sep 2014 at 11:24 pm</a> 
            </div> 
            <p>Due to the long deprecated practice of browser sniffing user agent strings tends to show the whole lineage of the Web. “Epiphany” is clearly indicated in our string, and so does the fact that we’re using WebKit, the engine that Apple derived from KHTML, which in turn presented itself to be “like Gecko”, the Mozilla engine when it still was Netscape.</p> 
           </div> 
           <ul class="children">

                   <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/8910056e0eab3f768555521d5923a1df?s=32&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/8910056e0eab3f768555521d5923a1df?s=64&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-32 photo" height="32" width="32"> 
                   <cite class="fn">sam</cite> 
                   <span class="says">says:</span> 
                  </div> 
                  <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
                   <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1008863"> 5th Sep 2014 at 1:12 pm</a> 
                  </div> 
                  <p>It says “Macintosh” and “Mac OS X”. Anyone trying to work out visitor statistics or offer an appropriate download of a file is going to count that as a Mac. The only way you can see that it is Linux is if you explicitly search for “Debian”.</p> 
                 </div> </li>
                <!-- #comment-## --> 
               </ul>

            <p>If you’re using VNC, no browser’s going to be very whizzy – there’s compression and decompression going on, and you may not be able to take advantage of the hardware acceleration. Why are you using a browser over VNC?</p> 
           </div> 
           <ul class="children">

          <p>I miss an ‘open image in new tab’. In my school workshop tutorials, there are a lot of 50% sized images and I have told the kids to ‘open in new tab’ when needing better readability. With this browser, ‘open image’ just downloads them to bottom line. When opening these iconized views, they get opened by ‘netsurf’, another browser in raspbian world.<br> Are there improvements planned in this area ?<br> Similiar topic for scratch applications. As mentioned above, I have links from my web pages to sample solutions in scratch. These are “scratch.sb” files, which open in scratch application nicely in midori, but not in this browser.</p>

             <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/7e0ba0ab7fa8d01703cecbe0bd972429?s=32&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/7e0ba0ab7fa8d01703cecbe0bd972429?s=64&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-32 photo" height="32" width="32">

             <span class="says">says:</span> 
            </div> 
            <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
             <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1009658"> 6th Sep 2014 at 1:25 pm</a> 
            </div> 
            <p>Hi Georgio,<br> This is not a problem.<br> If you put cgroup_enable=memory in to cmdline.txt this warning will go away, I believe it allows programs to handle memory more efficiently. Unfortunately for me it causes Epiphany to crash occasionally.<br> Regards,<br> Kevin.</p> 
           </div> 
           <ul class="children"> 
            <li class="comment odd alt depth-3" id="comment-1010004"> 
             <div id="div-comment-1010004" class="comment-body"> 
              <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
               <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/15e962dca62ab3548b70a48ad264e925?s=32&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/15e962dca62ab3548b70a48ad264e925?s=64&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-32 photo" height="32" width="32"> 
               <cite class="fn">Georgio M</cite> 
               <span class="says">says:</span> 
              </div> 
              <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
               <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1010004"> 6th Sep 2014 at 10:32 pm</a> 
              </div> 
              <p>Kevin,</p> 
              <p>Thank you for the help, sir. Some good news for you, it looks like the fine folks at Collabora pushed out a fix for the video and crash issue. After one more apt-get update &amp; dist-upgrade plus following your advise, I’m on about hour two of tooling around in Epiphany without a single crash.</p> 
              <p>If anyone else is wondering where to find <code>cmdline.txt</code>, it will be in <code>/boot</code>.</p> 
              <p>You can edit it by opening LXTerminal and typing in:</p> 
              <p><code>sudo nano /boot/cmdline.txt</code></p> 
              <p>In my case, everything had to go on the same line in order to work properly so put <code>cgroup_enable=memory</code> on the same line after everything else.</p> 
             </div> </li>

        <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" id="comment-1026336"> 
         <div id="div-comment-1026336" class="comment-body"> 
          <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
           <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d805974001d4481945cde5b938007a8b?s=32&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/d805974001d4481945cde5b938007a8b?s=64&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-32 photo" height="32" width="32"> 
           <cite class="fn">roses</cite> 
           <span class="says">says:</span> 
          </div> 
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1026336"> 27th Sep 2014 at 9:25 am</a> 
          </div> 
          <p>Well excuse me everyone, but this all-singing/all-dancing “new” browser doesn’t cut it for me.</p> 
          <p>Forgive my innocence, but isn’t one of the first things a noob wants to do with his/her Raspberry Pi is play You Tube videos??</p> 
          <p>I followed the install instructions carefully (update, dist-upgrade, install epiphany-browser, reboot) but when I go to ANY You Tube video it says (albeit very briefly and usually only on Page Reload) a plug-in is missing. Sure, the first frame as a still picture shows, but on pressing ‘Play’ the screen goes black and the progress bar doesn’t move.</p> 
          <p>I go to youtube.com/html5 to activate HTML5, but no difference. Even worse, I cannot find ANYWHERE in the Settings menu of Epiphany where I can install a plug-in or where to download that file from.</p> 
          <p>Sorry to all you guys, but I feel you’ve been wasting your time developing this if it doesn’t work OUT OF THE BOX and first time for all those of us who have no or very limited Linux experience.</p> 
          <p>It doesn’t even play the video on the main page of the raspberrypi.org website but instead gives the message ‘Aaargh, this video cannot be played with the current setup”.</p> 
          <p>Just as info, I have a brand new Model B-plus, connected via an HDMI-DVI adaptor into a Dell monitor. It’s a fresh install of Wheezy Raspbian, all updated, firmware updated, rpi-updated.</p> 
          <p>Since I’ve had my Pi during the last two weeks I’ve tried Midori, Chromium, Firefox (aka Ice Weasel) but NONE of them can play You Tube videos.</p> 
          <p>I’ve tried the same browsers in fresh installs of other distros, all with the same end result: YT does not work.</p> 
          <p>Sure, the R-Pi can play high definition videos from a USB stick or streaming from the internet, but personally I don’t see the point of it if it cannot pass this one basic test and playback a video from YT.</p> 
          <p>Perhaps I have something wrongly set up or there is a fault with my Pi – in which case I apologise and -I retract my rant. In which case, please point me in the right direction and show me what I’m doing wrong.</p> 
         </div> </li>

             <ul class="children"> 
              <li class="comment even depth-4" id="comment-1152120"> 
               <div id="div-comment-1152120" class="comment-body"> 
                <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
                 <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/392fe05c635da16f6cb3b5405c5e5bc8?s=32&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/392fe05c635da16f6cb3b5405c5e5bc8?s=64&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-32 photo" height="32" width="32"> 
                 <cite class="fn">KEV</cite> 
                 <span class="says">says:</span> 
                </div> 
                <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
                 <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1152120"> 7th Dec 2014 at 9:01 am</a> 
                </div> 
                <p>There are some factors to slow loading webpages and choppy online video streaming. One, use Raspbian for R-pi O.S. and Epiphany or Google Chrome for web browser, obviously. Two, overclock R-pi to the max (which is 1.0 GHz). Three, get the most fastest SD card available to date. After that, you will see much better improvements than before. </p> 
                <p>P.S. Regardless of all these steps taking, there will be some websites that are just JavaScript-heavy sites, embedded advertisements, loading images and gifs, etc. which will hinder the performance. And online video streaming can only be up to 720p at the moment.</p> 
               </div> </li>

          <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
           <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/357a20e8c56e69d6f9734d23ef9517e8?s=32&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/357a20e8c56e69d6f9734d23ef9517e8?s=64&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-32 photo" height="32" width="32"> 
           <cite class="fn">Brian</cite> 
           <span class="says">says:</span> 
          </div> 
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1198042"> 1st Feb 2015 at 7:46 am</a> 
          </div> 
          <p>Hi Seb,</p> 
          <p>The Epiphany Web Browser for Raspberry Pi can go full screen. When you are at the page you want, just push the F11 key and the page will go full screen, hiding the desktop menu bar and the browser URL bars. Another press of F11 brings the menus and bars back to normal.</p> 
         </div> </li>

        <li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1" id="comment-1198049">

           <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/357a20e8c56e69d6f9734d23ef9517e8?s=32&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/357a20e8c56e69d6f9734d23ef9517e8?s=64&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-32 photo" height="32" width="32">

          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1198049"> 1st Feb 2015 at 7:54 am</a> 
          </div> 
          <p>Hi Cyrus,</p> 
          <p>These two links should help guide you to changing that aspect:</p> 
          <p><a href="http://www.raspberrypi.org/forums/viewtopic.php?f=29&amp;t=43932" rel="nofollow">http://www.raspberrypi.org/forums/viewtopic.php?f=29&amp;t=43932</a><br> <a href="http://www.raspberrypi.org/forums/viewtopic.php?f=66&amp;t=18200" rel="nofollow">http://www.raspberrypi.org/forums/viewtopic.php?f=66&amp;t=18200</a></p> 
          <p>There’s a small tweak to stop screen save/blanking mode if you’re in the console mode (links show various methods).</p> 
          <p>Installing xscreensaver is a very easy way of doing it if you’re in the X Windows environment (the graphical icon based desktop you get with Raspian :] ). Once installed the settings are in your start menu to tinker with to your satisfaction!</p> 
          <p>Good luck.</p> 
         </div> </li>

           <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/0283332c3c79c1a52967bc98dede507d?s=32&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/0283332c3c79c1a52967bc98dede507d?s=64&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-32 photo" height="32" width="32"> 
           <cite class="fn">Glenn</cite> 
           <span class="says">says:</span> 
          </div> 
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1209228"> 23rd Feb 2015 at 3:29 am</a> 
          </div> 
          <p>Somehere i learned that class 4 is the highest supported by my Pi 2B. Somewhere I learned that SD cards go backward compatible to class I if you use a class not supported by your machine. If this is true it might explain the problems with the faster is better using class 10 when class 4 is what works best and gives the fastest results. That having been said Does raspberry PI sell 64 GB class 4 SD Card with noobs installed?<br> Or is there a rom upgrade that fixes this problem?</p> 
          <p>If I am wrong please delete this post.</p> 
          <p>Thanks!</p> 
         </div> </li>
        <!-- #comment-## --> 
        <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" id="comment-1209231"> 
         <div id="div-comment-1209231" class="comment-body"> 
          <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
           <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/0283332c3c79c1a52967bc98dede507d?s=32&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/0283332c3c79c1a52967bc98dede507d?s=64&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-32 photo" height="32" width="32"> 
           <cite class="fn">Glenn</cite> 
           <span class="says">says:</span> 
          </div> 
          <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
           <a href="https://www.raspberrypi.org/blog/web-browser-released/#comment-1209231"> 23rd Feb 2015 at 3:47 am</a> 
          </div> 
          <p>I forgot that i am running 16GB and 3 OS’es raspberian, boot to scratch which is a waste of memory since scratch is in raspberrian, and Elec.<br> That gives me 3 gb clearance. The browser is very nimble as long as i do not give it too many tabs/windows to keep track of. It sitll works as well as IE or chrome or FireFox but handles fewer browser tabs. And the SSH problem i mentioned before. </p> 
          <p>GOOD WORK ALL!</p> 
         </div> </li>
